]2;man cal]1;[?1049h[22;0;0t[32;1H[?1h=[4mCAL[24m(1)                                                                                        User Commands                                                                                        [4mCAL[24m(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       cal - display a calendar[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mcal [22m[options] [[[[4mday[24m] [4mmonth[24m] [4myear[24m][m
[m
       [1mcal [22m[options] [[4mtimestamp[24m|[4mmonthname[24m][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       [1mcal [22mdisplays a simple calendar. If no arguments are specified, the current month is displayed.[m
[m
       The [4mmonth[24m may be specified as a number (1-12), as a month name or as an abbreviated month name according to the current locales.[m
[m
       Two different calendar systems are used, Gregorian and Julian. These are nearly identical systems with Gregorian making a small adjustment to the frequency of leap years; this facilitates[m
       improved synchronization with solar events like the equinoxes. The Gregorian calendar reform was introduced in 1582, but its adoption continued up to 1923. By default [1mcal [22muses the adoption date[m
       of 3 Sept 1752. From that date forward the Gregorian calendar is displayed; previous dates use the Julian calendar system. 11 days were removed at the time of adoption to bring the calendar in[m
       sync with solar events. So Sept 1752 has a mix of Julian and Gregorian dates by which the 2nd is followed by the 14th (the 3rd through the 13th are absent).[m
[m
       Optionally, either the proleptic Gregorian calendar or the Julian calendar may be used exclusively. See [1m--reform [22mbelow.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       [1m-1[22m, [1m--one[0m[m
           Display single month output. (This is the default.)[m
[m
       [1m-3[22m, [1m--three[0m[m
           Display three months spanning the date.[m
[m
       [1m-n , --months [4m[22mnumber[0m[m
           Display [4mnumber[24m of months, starting from the month containing the date.[m

[1mNAME[0m[m
       ls - list directory contents[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mls [22m[[4mOPTION[24m]... [[4mFILE[24m]...[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       List information about the FILEs (the current directory by default).  Sort entries alphabetically if none of [1m-cftuvSUX [22mnor [1m--sort [22mis specified.[m
[m
       Mandatory arguments to long options are mandatory for short options too.[m
[m
       [1m-a[22m, [1m--all[0m[m
              do not ignore entries starting with .[m
[m
       [1m-A[22m, [1m--almost-all[0m[m
              do not list implied . and ..[m
[m
       [1m--author[0m[m
              with [1m-l[22m, print the author of each file[m
[m
       [1m-b[22m, [1m--escape[0m[m
              print C-style escapes for nongraphic characters[m
[m
       [1m--block-size[22m=[4mSIZE[0m[m
              with [1m-l[22m, scale sizes by SIZE when printing them; e.g., '--block-size=M'; see SIZE format below[m
[m
       [1m-B[22m, [1m--ignore-backups[0m[m
              do not list implied entries ending with ~[m
[m

[1;32m‚ùØ[0m [K[?2004h[7m[32mman[39m[7m wc[27m[27m[32mm[27m[32ma[27m[32mn[39m[27m [27mw[27mc[?2004l
]2;man wc]1;[?1049h[22;0;0t[32;1H[?1h=[4mWC[24m(1)                                                                                         User Commands                                                                                         [4mWC[24m(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       wc - print newline, word, and byte counts for each file[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mwc [22m[[4mOPTION[24m]... [[4mFILE[24m]...[m
       [1mwc [22m[[4mOPTION[24m]... [4m--files0-from=F[0m[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       Print  newline, word, and byte counts for each FILE, and a total line if more than one FILE is specified.  A word is a nonempty sequence of non white space delimited by white space characters or[m
       by start or end of input.[m
[m
       With no FILE, or when FILE is -, read standard input.[m
[m
       The options below may be used to select which counts are printed, always in the following order: newline, word, character, byte, maximum line length.[m
[m
       [1m-c[22m, [1m--bytes[0m[m
              print the byte counts[m
[m
       [1m-m[22m, [1m--chars[0m[m
              print the character counts[m
[m
       [1m-l[22m, [1m--lines[0m[m
              print the newline counts[m
[m
       [1m--files0-from[22m=[4mF[0m[m
              read input from the files specified by NUL-terminated names in file F; If F is - then read names from standard input[m
[m
       [1m-L[22m, [1m--max-line-length[0m[m
              print the maximum display width[m
[01;47;34m Manual page wc(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page wc(1) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K       [1m-w[22m, [1m--words[0m[m
[01;47;34m Manual page wc(1) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K              print the word counts[m
[01;47;34m Manual page wc(1) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page wc(1) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K       [1m--total[22m=[4mWHEN[0m[m
[01;47;34m Manual page wc(1) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K              when to print a line with total counts; WHEN can be: auto, always, only, never[m
[01;47;34m Manual page wc(1) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K[m

[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m

           [--exec-path[=<path>]] [--html-path] [--man-path] [--info-path][m

[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       Git is a fast, scalable, distributed revision control system with an unusually rich command set that provides both high-level operations and full access to internals.[m
[m
       See [1mgittutorial[22m(7) to get started, then see [1mgiteveryday[22m(7) for a useful minimum set of commands. The [34m[1mGit User‚Äôs Manual[0m[1m[22m[1] has a more in-depth introduction.[m
[m
       After you mastered the basic concepts, you can come back to this page to learn what commands Git offers. You can learn more about individual Git commands with "git help command". [1mgitcli[22m(7)[m
       manual page gives you an overview of the command-line command syntax.[m
[m
       A formatted and hyperlinked copy of the latest Git documentation can be viewed at [34m[1mhttps://git.github.io/htmldocs/git.html [0m[1m[22mor [34m[1mhttps://git-scm.com/docs[0m[1m[22m.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       -v, --version[m
           Prints the Git suite version that the [4mgit[24m program came from.[m
[m
           This option is internally converted to [1mgit version [22m... and accepts the same options as the [1mgit-version[22m(1) command. If [1m--help [22mis also given, it takes precedence over [1m--version[22m.[m
[m
       -h, --help[m
           Prints the synopsis and a list of the most commonly used commands. If the option [1m--all [22mor [1m-a [22mis given then all available commands are printed. If a Git command is named this option will[m

]2;man git]1;[?1049h[22;0;0t[32;1H[?1h=[4mGIT[24m(1)                                                                                          Git Manual                                                                                         [4mGIT[24m(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       git - the stupid content tracker[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [4mgit[24m [-v | --version] [-h | --help] [-C <path>] [-c <name>=<value>][m
           [--exec-path[=<path>]] [--html-path] [--man-path] [--info-path][m
           [-p | --paginate | -P | --no-pager] [--no-replace-objects] [--no-lazy-fetch][m
           [--no-optional-locks] [--no-advice] [--bare] [--git-dir=<path>][m
           [--work-tree=<path>] [--namespace=<name>] [--config-env=<name>=<envvar>][m
           <command> [<args>][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       Git is a fast, scalable, distributed revision control system with an unusually rich command set that provides both high-level operations and full access to internals.[m
[m
       See [1mgittutorial[22m(7) to get started, then see [1mgiteveryday[22m(7) for a useful minimum set of commands. The [34m[1mGit User‚Äôs Manual[0m[1m[22m[1] has a more in-depth introduction.[m
[m
       After you mastered the basic concepts, you can come back to this page to learn what commands Git offers. You can learn more about individual Git commands with "git help command". [1mgitcli[22m(7)[m
       manual page gives you an overview of the command-line command syntax.[m
[m
       A formatted and hyperlinked copy of the latest Git documentation can be viewed at [34m[1mhttps://git.github.io/htmldocs/git.html [0m[1m[22mor [34m[1mhttps://git-scm.com/docs[0m[1m[22m.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       -v, --version[m
           Prints the Git suite version that the [4mgit[24m program came from.[m
[m
           This option is internally converted to [1mgit version [22m... and accepts the same options as the [1mgit-version[22m(1) command. If [1m--help [22mis also given, it takes precedence over [1m--version[22m.[m
[m
       -h, --help[m
           Prints the synopsis and a list of the most commonly used commands. If the option [1m--all [22mor [1m-a [22mis given then all available commands are printed. If a Git command is named this option will[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           bring up the manual page for that command.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           Other options are available to control how the manual page is displayed. See [1mgit-help[22m(1) for more information, because [1mgit --help [22m... is converted internally into [1mgit help [22m....[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       -C <path>[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           Run as if git was started in [4m<path>[24m instead of the current working directory. When multiple [1m-C [22moptions are given, each subsequent non-absolute [1m-C [4m[22m<path>[24m is interpreted relative to the[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           preceding [1m-C [4m[22m<path>[24m. If [4m<path>[24m is present but empty, e.g.  [1m-C [22m"", then the current working directory is left unchanged.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 8 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 9 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           This option affects options that expect path name like [1m--git-dir [22mand [1m--work-tree [22min that their interpretations of the path names would be made relative to the working directory caused by the[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 10 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           [1m-C [22moption. For example the following invocations are equivalent:[m

[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           directly setting the value to an empty string, instead the environment variable itself must be set to the empty string. It is an error if the [4m<envvar>[24m does not exist in the environment.[m

]2;man git]1;[?1049h[22;0;0t[32;1H[?1h=[4mGIT[24m(1)                                                                                          Git Manual                                                                                         [4mGIT[24m(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       git - the stupid content tracker[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [4mgit[24m [-v | --version] [-h | --help] [-C <path>] [-c <name>=<value>][m
           [--exec-path[=<path>]] [--html-path] [--man-path] [--info-path][m
           [-p | --paginate | -P | --no-pager] [--no-replace-objects] [--no-lazy-fetch][m
           [--no-optional-locks] [--no-advice] [--bare] [--git-dir=<path>][m
           [--work-tree=<path>] [--namespace=<name>] [--config-env=<name>=<envvar>][m
           <command> [<args>][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       Git is a fast, scalable, distributed revision control system with an unusually rich command set that provides both high-level operations and full access to internals.[m
[m
       See [1mgittutorial[22m(7) to get started, then see [1mgiteveryday[22m(7) for a useful minimum set of commands. The [34m[1mGit User‚Äôs Manual[0m[1m[22m[1] has a more in-depth introduction.[m
[m
       After you mastered the basic concepts, you can come back to this page to learn what commands Git offers. You can learn more about individual Git commands with "git help command". [1mgitcli[22m(7)[m
       manual page gives you an overview of the command-line command syntax.[m
[m
       A formatted and hyperlinked copy of the latest Git documentation can be viewed at [34m[1mhttps://git.github.io/htmldocs/git.html [0m[1m[22mor [34m[1mhttps://git-scm.com/docs[0m[1m[22m.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       -v, --version[m
           Prints the Git suite version that the [4mgit[24m program came from.[m
[m
           This option is internally converted to [1mgit version [22m... and accepts the same options as the [1mgit-version[22m(1) command. If [1m--help [22mis also given, it takes precedence over [1m--version[22m.[m
[m
       -h, --help[m
           Prints the synopsis and a list of the most commonly used commands. If the option [1m--all [22mor [1m-a [22mis given then all available commands are printed. If a Git command is named this option will[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           bring up the manual page for that command.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 3 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           Other options are available to control how the manual page is displayed. See [1mgit-help[22m(1) for more information, because [1mgit --help [22m... is converted internally into [1mgit help [22m....[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 4 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       -C <path>[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           Run as if git was started in [4m<path>[24m instead of the current working directory. When multiple [1m-C [22moptions are given, each subsequent non-absolute [1m-C [4m[22m<path>[24m is interpreted relative to the[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           preceding [1m-C [4m[22m<path>[24m. If [4m<path>[24m is present but empty, e.g.  [1m-C [22m"", then the current working directory is left unchanged.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 8 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 9 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           This option affects options that expect path name like [1m--git-dir [22mand [1m--work-tree [22min that their interpretations of the path names would be made relative to the working directory caused by the[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 10 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           [1m-C [22moption. For example the following invocations are equivalent:[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 11 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 12 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               git --git-dir=a.git --work-tree=b -C c status[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 13 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K               git --git-dir=c/a.git --work-tree=c/b status[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 14 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 15 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       -c <name>=<value>[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 16 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           Pass a configuration parameter to the command. The value given will override values from configuration files. The <name> is expected in the same format as listed by [4mgit[24m [4mconfig[24m (subkeys[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 17 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           separated by dots).[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 18 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 19 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           Note that omitting the [1m= [22min [1mgit -c foo.bar [22m... is allowed and sets [1mfoo.bar [22mto the boolean true value (just like [[1mfoo[22m][1mbar [22mwould in a config file). Including the equals but with an empty value[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 20 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           (like [1mgit -c foo.bar= [22m...) sets [1mfoo.bar [22mto the empty string which [1mgit config --type=bool [22mwill convert to [1mfalse[22m.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 21 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 22 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       --config-env=<name>=<envvar>[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 23 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           Like [1m-c [4m[22m<name>[24m[1m=[4m[22m<value>[24m, give configuration variable [4m<name>[24m a value, where <envvar> is the name of an environment variable from which to retrieve the value. Unlike [1m-c [22mthere is no shortcut for[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 24 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           directly setting the value to an empty string, instead the environment variable itself must be set to the empty string. It is an error if the [4m<envvar>[24m does not exist in the environment.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 25 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           [4m<envvar>[24m may not contain an equals sign to avoid ambiguity with [4m<name>[24m containing one.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 26 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 27 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           This is useful for cases where you want to pass transitory configuration options to git, but are doing so on operating systems where other processes might be able to read your command line[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 28 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           (e.g.  [1m/proc/self/cmdline[22m), but not your environment (e.g.  [1m/proc/self/environ[22m). That behavior is the default on Linux, but may not be on your system.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 29 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 30 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           Note that this might add security for variables such as [1mhttp.extraHeader [22mwhere the sensitive information is part of the value, but not e.g.  [1murl.[4m[22m<base>[24m[1m.insteadOf [22mwhere the sensitive[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 31 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           information can be part of the key.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 32 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 33 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       --exec-path[=<path>][m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 34 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           Path to wherever your core Git programs are installed. This can also be controlled by setting the GIT_EXEC_PATH environment variable. If no path is given, [4mgit[24m will print the current setting[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 35 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K           and then exit.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 36 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 37 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       --html-path[m

   [1mReset, restore and revert[0m[m
       There are three commands with similar names: [1mgit reset[22m, [1mgit restore [22mand [1mgit revert[22m.[m
[m
       ‚Ä¢   [1mgit-revert[22m(1) is about making a new commit that reverts the changes made by other commits.[m
[m
       ‚Ä¢   [1mgit-restore[22m(1) is about restoring files in the working tree from either the index or another commit. This command does not update your branch. The command can also be used to restore files[m
           in the index from another commit.[m
[m
       ‚Ä¢   [1mgit-reset[22m(1) is about updating your branch, moving the tip in order to add or remove commits from the branch. This operation changes the commit history.[m
[m
           [1mgit reset [22mcan also be used to restore the index, overlapping with [1mgit restore[22m.[m
[m
[1mLOW-LEVEL COMMANDS (PLUMBING)[0m[m
       Although Git includes its own porcelain layer, its low-level commands are sufficient to support development of alternative porcelains. Developers of such porcelains might start by reading about[m
       [1mgit-update-index[22m(1) and [1mgit-read-tree[22m(1).[m
[m
       The interface (input, output, set of options and the semantics) to these low-level commands are meant to be a lot more stable than Porcelain level commands, because these commands are primarily[m
       for scripted use. The interface to Porcelain commands on the other hand are subject to change in order to improve the end user experience.[m
[m
       The following description divides the low-level commands into commands that manipulate objects (in the repository, index, and working tree), commands that interrogate and compare objects, and[m
       commands that move objects and references between repositories.[m
[m
   [1mManipulation commands[0m[m
       [1mgit-apply[22m(1)[m

[m

[1mCONFIGURATION MECHANISM[0m[m
       Git uses a simple text format to store customizations that are per repository and are per user. Such a configuration file may look like this:[m
[m
           #[m
           # A '#' or ';' character indicates a comment.[m
           #[m
[m
           ; core variables[m
           [core][m
                   ; Don't trust file modes[m
                   filemode = false[m
[m
           ; user identity[m
           [user][m
                   name = "Junio C Hamano"[m
                   email = "gitster@pobox.com"[m
[m
       Various commands read from the configuration file and adjust their operation accordingly. See [1mgit-config[22m(1) for a list and more details about the configuration mechanism.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 739 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
[1mIDENTIFIER TERMINOLOGY[0m[m
       <object>[m
           Indicates the object name for any type of object.[m
[m
       <blob>[m
           Indicates a blob object name.[m
[m
       <tree>[m
           Indicates a tree object name.[m
[m
       <commit>[m
           Indicates a commit object name.[m
[m
       <tree-ish>[m
           Indicates a tree, commit or tag object name. A command that takes a <tree-ish> argument ultimately wants to operate on a <tree> object but automatically dereferences <commit> and <tag>[m
           objects that point at a <tree>.[m
[m
       <commit-ish>[m
           Indicates a commit or tag object name. A command that takes a <commit-ish> argument ultimately wants to operate on a <commit> object but automatically dereferences <tag> objects that point[m
           at a <commit>.[m
[m
       <type>[m
           Indicates that an object type is required. Currently one of: [1mblob[22m, [1mtree[22m, [1mcommit[22m, or [1mtag[22m.[m
[m
       <file>[m
           Indicates a filename - almost always relative to the root of the tree structure [1mGIT_INDEX_FILE [22mdescribes.[m
[m
[1mSYMBOLIC IDENTIFIERS[0m[m
       Any Git command accepting any <object> can also use the following symbolic notation:[m
[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 770 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       HEAD[m
           indicates the head of the current branch.[m
[m
       <tag>[m
           a valid tag [4mname[24m (i.e. a [1mrefs/tags/[4m[22m<tag>[24m reference).[m
[m
       <head>[m
           a valid head [4mname[24m (i.e. a [1mrefs/heads/[4m[22m<head>[24m reference).[m
[m
       For a more complete list of ways to spell object names, see "SPECIFYING REVISIONS" section in [1mgitrevisions[22m(7).[m
[m

[m
       Higher level SCMs may provide and manage additional information in the [1m$GIT_DIR[22m.[m

[1mENVIRONMENT VARIABLES[0m[m
       Various Git commands pay attention to environment variables and change their behavior. The environment variables marked as "Boolean" take their values the same way as Boolean valued[m
       configuration variables, i.e., "true", "yes", "on" and positive numbers are taken as "yes", while "false", "no", "off", and "0" are taken as "no".[m
[m
       Here are the variables:[m
[m
   [1mSystem[0m[m
       [1mHOME[0m[m
           Specifies the path to the user‚Äôs home directory. On Windows, if unset, Git will set a process environment variable equal to: [1m$HOMEDRIVE$HOMEPATH [22mif both [1m$HOMEDRIVE [22mand [1m$HOMEPATH [22mexist;[m
           otherwise [1m$USERPROFILE [22mif [1m$USERPROFILE [22mexists.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 801 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
   [1mThe Git Repository[0m[m
       These environment variables apply to [4mall[24m core Git commands. Nb: it is worth noting that they may be used/overridden by SCMS sitting above Git so take care if using a foreign front-end.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_INDEX_FILE[0m[m
           This environment variable specifies an alternate index file. If not specified, the default of [1m$GIT_DIR/index [22mis used.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_INDEX_VERSION[0m[m
           This environment variable specifies what index version is used when writing the index file out. It won‚Äôt affect existing index files. By default index file version 2 or 3 is used. See [1mgit-[0m[m
           [1mupdate-index[22m(1) for more information.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_OBJECT_DIRECTORY[0m[m
           If the object storage directory is specified via this environment variable then the sha1 directories are created underneath - otherwise the default [1m$GIT_DIR/objects [22mdirectory is used.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_ALTERNATE_OBJECT_DIRECTORIES[0m[m
           Due to the immutable nature of Git objects, old objects can be archived into shared, read-only directories. This variable specifies a ":" separated (on Windows ";" separated) list of Git[m
           object directories which can be used to search for Git objects. New objects will not be written to these directories.[m
[m
           Entries that begin with " (double-quote) will be interpreted as C-style quoted paths, removing leading and trailing double-quotes and respecting backslash escapes. E.g., the value[m
           "path-with-\"-and-:-in-it":vanilla-path has two paths: [1mpath-with-[22m"-and-:-in-it and [1mvanilla-path[22m.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_DIR[0m[m
           If the [1mGIT_DIR [22menvironment variable is set then it specifies a path to use instead of the default [1m.git [22mfor the base of the repository. The [1m--git-dir [22mcommand-line option also sets this value.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_WORK_TREE[0m[m
           Set the path to the root of the working tree. This can also be controlled by the [1m--work-tree [22mcommand-line option and the core.worktree configuration variable.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_NAMESPACE[0m[m
           Set the Git namespace; see [1mgitnamespaces[22m(7) for details. The [1m--namespace [22mcommand-line option also sets this value.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_CEILING_DIRECTORIES[0m[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 832 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K           This should be a colon-separated list of absolute paths. If set, it is a list of directories that Git should not chdir up into while looking for a repository directory (useful for excluding[m
           slow-loading network directories). It will not exclude the current working directory or a GIT_DIR set on the command line or in the environment. Normally, Git has to read the entries in this[m
           list and resolve any symlink that might be present in order to compare them with the current directory. However, if even this access is slow, you can add an empty entry to the list to tell[m
           Git that the subsequent entries are not symlinks and needn‚Äôt be resolved; e.g., [1mGIT_CEILING_DIRECTORIES=/maybe/symlink::/very/slow/non/symlink[22m.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_DISCOVERY_ACROSS_FILESYSTEM[0m[m
           When run in a directory that does not have ".git" repository directory, Git tries to find such a directory in the parent directories to find the top of the working tree, but by default it[m
           does not cross filesystem boundaries. This Boolean environment variable can be set to true to tell Git not to stop at filesystem boundaries. Like [1mGIT_CEILING_DIRECTORIES[22m, this will not[m
           affect an explicit repository directory set via [1mGIT_DIR [22mor on the command line.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_COMMON_DIR[0m[m
           If this variable is set to a path, non-worktree files that are normally in $GIT_DIR will be taken from this path instead. Worktree-specific files such as HEAD or index are taken from[m
           $GIT_DIR. See [1mgitrepository-layout[22m(5) and [1mgit-worktree[22m(1) for details. This variable has lower precedence than other path variables such as GIT_INDEX_FILE, GIT_OBJECT_DIRECTORY...[m
[m
       [1mGIT_DEFAULT_HASH[0m[m
           If this variable is set, the default hash algorithm for new repositories will be set to this value. This value is ignored when cloning and the setting of the remote repository is always[m
           used. The default is "sha1". See [1m--object-format [22min [1mgit-init[22m(1).[m
[m
       [1mGIT_DEFAULT_REF_FORMAT[0m[m
           If this variable is set, the default reference backend format for new repositories will be set to this value. The default is "files". See [1m--ref-format [22min [1mgit-init[22m(1).[m
[m
   [1mGit Commits[0m[m
       [1mGIT_AUTHOR_NAME[0m[m
           The human-readable name used in the author identity when creating commit or tag objects, or when writing reflogs. Overrides the [1muser.name [22mand [1mauthor.name [22mconfiguration settings.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_AUTHOR_EMAIL[0m[m
           The email address used in the author identity when creating commit or tag objects, or when writing reflogs. Overrides the [1muser.email [22mand [1mauthor.email [22mconfiguration settings.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_AUTHOR_DATE[0m[m
           The date used for the author identity when creating commit or tag objects, or when writing reflogs. See [1mgit-commit[22m(1) for valid formats.[m
[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 863 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       [1mGIT_COMMITTER_NAME[0m[m
           The human-readable name used in the committer identity when creating commit or tag objects, or when writing reflogs. Overrides the [1muser.name [22mand [1mcommitter.name [22mconfiguration settings.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_COMMITTER_EMAIL[0m[m
           The email address used in the author identity when creating commit or tag objects, or when writing reflogs. Overrides the [1muser.email [22mand [1mcommitter.email [22mconfiguration settings.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_COMMITTER_DATE[0m[m
           The date used for the committer identity when creating commit or tag objects, or when writing reflogs. See [1mgit-commit[22m(1) for valid formats.[m
[m
       [1mEMAIL[0m[m
           The email address used in the author and committer identities if no other relevant environment variable or configuration setting has been set.[m
[m
   [1mGit Diffs[0m[m
       [1mGIT_DIFF_OPTS[0m[m
           Only valid setting is "--unified=??" or "-u??" to set the number of context lines shown when a unified diff is created. This takes precedence over any "-U" or "--unified" option value passed[m
           on the Git diff command line.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_EXTERNAL_DIFF[0m[m
           When the environment variable [1mGIT_EXTERNAL_DIFF [22mis set, the program named by it is called to generate diffs, and Git does not use its builtin diff machinery. For a path that is added,[m
           removed, or modified, [1mGIT_EXTERNAL_DIFF [22mis called with 7 parameters:[m
[m
               path old-file old-hex old-mode new-file new-hex new-mode[m
[m
           where:[m
[m
       <old|new>-file[m
           are files GIT_EXTERNAL_DIFF can use to read the contents of <old|new>,[m
[m
       <old|new>-hex[m
           are the 40-hexdigit SHA-1 hashes,[m
[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 894 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       <old|new>-mode[m
           are the octal representation of the file modes.[m
[m
           The file parameters can point at the user‚Äôs working file (e.g.  [1mnew-file [22min "git-diff-files"), [1m/dev/null [22m(e.g.  [1mold-file [22mwhen a new file is added), or a temporary file (e.g.  [1mold-file [22min the[m
           index).  [1mGIT_EXTERNAL_DIFF [22mshould not worry about unlinking the temporary file ‚Äî it is removed when [1mGIT_EXTERNAL_DIFF [22mexits.[m
[m
           For a path that is unmerged, [1mGIT_EXTERNAL_DIFF [22mis called with 1 parameter, <path>.[m
[m
           For each path [1mGIT_EXTERNAL_DIFF [22mis called, two environment variables, [1mGIT_DIFF_PATH_COUNTER [22mand [1mGIT_DIFF_PATH_TOTAL [22mare set.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_EXTERNAL_DIFF_TRUST_EXIT_CODE[0m[m
           If this Boolean environment variable is set to true then the [1mGIT_EXTERNAL_DIFF [22mcommand is expected to return exit code 0 if it considers the input files to be equal or 1 if it considers them[m
           to be different, like [1mdiff[22m([1m1[22m). If it is set to false, which is the default, then the command is expected to return exit code 0 regardless of equality. Any other exit code causes Git to[m
           report a fatal error.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_DIFF_PATH_COUNTER[0m[m
           A 1-based counter incremented by one for every path.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_DIFF_PATH_TOTAL[0m[m
           The total number of paths.[m
[m
   [1mother[0m[m
       [1mGIT_MERGE_VERBOSITY[0m[m
           A number controlling the amount of output shown by the recursive merge strategy. Overrides merge.verbosity. See [1mgit-merge[22m(1)[m
[m
       [1mGIT_PAGER[0m[m
           This environment variable overrides [1m$PAGER[22m. If it is set to an empty string or to the value "cat", Git will not launch a pager. See also the [1mcore.pager [22moption in [1mgit-config[22m(1).[m
[m
       [1mGIT_PROGRESS_DELAY[0m[m
           A number controlling how many seconds to delay before showing optional progress indicators. Defaults to 2.[m
[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 925 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       [1mGIT_EDITOR[0m[m
           This environment variable overrides [1m$EDITOR [22mand [1m$VISUAL[22m. It is used by several Git commands when, on interactive mode, an editor is to be launched. See also [1mgit-var[22m(1) and the [1mcore.editor[0m[m
           option in [1mgit-config[22m(1).[m
[m
       [1mGIT_SEQUENCE_EDITOR[0m[m
           This environment variable overrides the configured Git editor when editing the todo list of an interactive rebase. See also [1mgit-rebase[22m(1) and the [1msequence.editor [22moption in [1mgit-config[22m(1).[m
[m
       [1mGIT_SSH[22m, [1mGIT_SSH_COMMAND[0m[m
           If either of these environment variables is set then [4mgit[24m [4mfetch[24m and [4mgit[24m [4mpush[24m will use the specified command instead of [4mssh[24m when they need to connect to a remote system. The command-line[m
           parameters passed to the configured command are determined by the ssh variant. See [1mssh.variant [22moption in [1mgit-config[22m(1) for details.[m
[m
           [1m$GIT_SSH_COMMAND [22mtakes precedence over [1m$GIT_SSH[22m, and is interpreted by the shell, which allows additional arguments to be included.  [1m$GIT_SSH [22mon the other hand must be just the path to a[m
           program (which can be a wrapper shell script, if additional arguments are needed).[m
[m
           Usually it is easier to configure any desired options through your personal [1m.ssh/config [22mfile. Please consult your ssh documentation for further details.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_SSH_VARIANT[0m[m
           If this environment variable is set, it overrides Git‚Äôs autodetection whether [1mGIT_SSH[22m/[1mGIT_SSH_COMMAND[22m/[1mcore.sshCommand [22mrefer to OpenSSH, plink or tortoiseplink. This variable overrides the[m
           config setting [1mssh.variant [22mthat serves the same purpose.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_SSL_NO_VERIFY[0m[m
           Setting and exporting this environment variable to any value tells Git not to verify the SSL certificate when fetching or pushing over HTTPS.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_ATTR_SOURCE[0m[m
           Sets the treeish that gitattributes will be read from.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_ASKPASS[0m[m
           If this environment variable is set, then Git commands which need to acquire passwords or passphrases (e.g. for HTTP or IMAP authentication) will call this program with a suitable prompt as[m
           command-line argument and read the password from its STDOUT. See also the [1mcore.askPass [22moption in [1mgit-config[22m(1).[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TERMINAL_PROMPT[0m[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 956 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K           If this Boolean environment variable is set to false, git will not prompt on the terminal (e.g., when asking for HTTP authentication).[m
[m
       [1mGIT_CONFIG_GLOBAL[22m, [1mGIT_CONFIG_SYSTEM[0m[m
           Take the configuration from the given files instead from global or system-level configuration files. If [1mGIT_CONFIG_SYSTEM [22mis set, the system config file defined at build time (usually[m
           [1m/etc/gitconfig[22m) will not be read. Likewise, if [1mGIT_CONFIG_GLOBAL [22mis set, neither [1m$HOME/.gitconfig [22mnor [1m$XDG_CONFIG_HOME/git/config [22mwill be read. Can be set to [1m/dev/null [22mto skip reading[m
           configuration files of the respective level.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_CONFIG_NOSYSTEM[0m[m
           Whether to skip reading settings from the system-wide [1m$[22m([1mprefix[22m)[1m/etc/gitconfig [22mfile. This Boolean environment variable can be used along with [1m$HOME [22mand [1m$XDG_CONFIG_HOME [22mto create a[m
           predictable environment for a picky script, or you can set it to true to temporarily avoid using a buggy [1m/etc/gitconfig [22mfile while waiting for someone with sufficient permissions to fix it.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_FLUSH[0m[m
           If this Boolean environment variable is set to true, then commands such as [4mgit[24m [4mblame[24m (in incremental mode), [4mgit[24m [4mrev-list[24m, [4mgit[24m [4mlog[24m, [4mgit[24m [4mcheck-attr[24m and [4mgit[24m [4mcheck-ignore[24m will force a flush of[m
           the output stream after each record have been flushed. If this variable is set to false, the output of these commands will be done using completely buffered I/O. If this environment variable[m
           is not set, Git will choose buffered or record-oriented flushing based on whether stdout appears to be redirected to a file or not.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE[0m[m
           Enables general trace messages, e.g. alias expansion, built-in command execution and external command execution.[m
[m
           If this variable is set to "1", "2" or "true" (comparison is case insensitive), trace messages will be printed to stderr.[m
[m
           If the variable is set to an integer value greater than 2 and lower than 10 (strictly) then Git will interpret this value as an open file descriptor and will try to write the trace messages[m
           into this file descriptor.[m
[m
           Alternatively, if the variable is set to an absolute path (starting with a [4m/[24m character), Git will interpret this as a file path and will try to append the trace messages to it.[m
[m
           Unsetting the variable, or setting it to empty, "0" or "false" (case insensitive) disables trace messages.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE_FSMONITOR[0m[m
           Enables trace messages for the filesystem monitor extension. See [1mGIT_TRACE [22mfor available trace output options.[m
[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 987 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       [1mGIT_TRACE_PACK_ACCESS[0m[m
           Enables trace messages for all accesses to any packs. For each access, the pack file name and an offset in the pack is recorded. This may be helpful for troubleshooting some pack-related[m
           performance problems. See [1mGIT_TRACE [22mfor available trace output options.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE_PACKET[0m[m
           Enables trace messages for all packets coming in or out of a given program. This can help with debugging object negotiation or other protocol issues. Tracing is turned off at a packet[m
           starting with "PACK" (but see [1mGIT_TRACE_PACKFILE [22mbelow). See [1mGIT_TRACE [22mfor available trace output options.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE_PACKFILE[0m[m
           Enables tracing of packfiles sent or received by a given program. Unlike other trace output, this trace is verbatim: no headers, and no quoting of binary data. You almost certainly want to[m
           direct into a file (e.g., [1mGIT_TRACE_PACKFILE=/tmp/my.pack[22m) rather than displaying it on the terminal or mixing it with other trace output.[m
[m
           Note that this is currently only implemented for the client side of clones and fetches.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE_PERFORMANCE[0m[m
           Enables performance related trace messages, e.g. total execution time of each Git command. See [1mGIT_TRACE [22mfor available trace output options.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE_REFS[0m[m
           Enables trace messages for operations on the ref database. See [1mGIT_TRACE [22mfor available trace output options.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE_SETUP[0m[m
           Enables trace messages printing the .git, working tree and current working directory after Git has completed its setup phase. See [1mGIT_TRACE [22mfor available trace output options.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE_SHALLOW[0m[m
           Enables trace messages that can help debugging fetching / cloning of shallow repositories. See [1mGIT_TRACE [22mfor available trace output options.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE_CURL[0m[m
           Enables a curl full trace dump of all incoming and outgoing data, including descriptive information, of the git transport protocol. This is similar to doing curl [1m--trace-ascii [22mon the command[m
           line. See [1mGIT_TRACE [22mfor available trace output options.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE_CURL_NO_DATA[0m[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 1018 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K           When a curl trace is enabled (see [1mGIT_TRACE_CURL [22mabove), do not dump data (that is, only dump info lines and headers).[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE2[0m[m
           Enables more detailed trace messages from the "trace2" library. Output from [1mGIT_TRACE2 [22mis a simple text-based format for human readability.[m
[m
           If this variable is set to "1", "2" or "true" (comparison is case insensitive), trace messages will be printed to stderr.[m
[m
           If the variable is set to an integer value greater than 2 and lower than 10 (strictly) then Git will interpret this value as an open file descriptor and will try to write the trace messages[m
           into this file descriptor.[m
[m
           Alternatively, if the variable is set to an absolute path (starting with a [4m/[24m character), Git will interpret this as a file path and will try to append the trace messages to it. If the path[m
           already exists and is a directory, the trace messages will be written to files (one per process) in that directory, named according to the last component of the SID and an optional counter[m
           (to avoid filename collisions).[m
[m
           In addition, if the variable is set to [1maf_unix:[22m[[4m<socket-type>[24m[1m:[22m][4m<absolute-pathname>[24m, Git will try to open the path as a Unix Domain Socket. The socket type can be either [1mstream [22mor [1mdgram[22m.[m
[m
           Unsetting the variable, or setting it to empty, "0" or "false" (case insensitive) disables trace messages.[m
[m
           See [34m[1mTrace2 documentation[0m[1m[22m[2] for full details.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE2_EVENT[0m[m
           This setting writes a JSON-based format that is suited for machine interpretation. See [1mGIT_TRACE2 [22mfor available trace output options and [34m[1mTrace2 documentation[0m[1m[22m[2] for full details.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE2_PERF[0m[m
           In addition to the text-based messages available in [1mGIT_TRACE2[22m, this setting writes a column-based format for understanding nesting regions. See [1mGIT_TRACE2 [22mfor available trace output options[m
           and [34m[1mTrace2 documentation[0m[1m[22m[2] for full details.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_TRACE_REDACT[0m[m
           By default, when tracing is activated, Git redacts the values of cookies, the "Authorization:" header, the "Proxy-Authorization:" header and packfile URIs. Set this Boolean environment[m
           variable to false to prevent this redaction.[m
[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 1049 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       [1mGIT_NO_REPLACE_OBJECTS[0m[m
           Setting and exporting this environment variable tells Git to ignore replacement refs and do not replace Git objects.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_LITERAL_PATHSPECS[0m[m
           Setting this Boolean environment variable to true will cause Git to treat all pathspecs literally, rather than as glob patterns. For example, running [1mGIT_LITERAL_PATHSPECS=1 git log -- [22m'*.c'[m
           will search for commits that touch the path *.c, not any paths that the glob *.c matches. You might want this if you are feeding literal paths to Git (e.g., paths previously given to you by[m
           [1mgit ls-tree[22m, [1m--raw [22mdiff output, etc).[m
[m
       [1mGIT_GLOB_PATHSPECS[0m[m
           Setting this Boolean environment variable to true will cause Git to treat all pathspecs as glob patterns (aka "glob" magic).[m
[m
       [1mGIT_NOGLOB_PATHSPECS[0m[m
           Setting this Boolean environment variable to true will cause Git to treat all pathspecs as literal (aka "literal" magic).[m
[m
       [1mGIT_ICASE_PATHSPECS[0m[m
           Setting this Boolean environment variable to true will cause Git to treat all pathspecs as case-insensitive.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_NO_LAZY_FETCH[0m[m
           Setting this Boolean environment variable to true tells Git not to lazily fetch missing objects from the promisor remote on demand.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_REFLOG_ACTION[0m[m
           When a ref is updated, reflog entries are created to keep track of the reason why the ref was updated (which is typically the name of the high-level command that updated the ref), in[m
           addition to the old and new values of the ref. A scripted Porcelain command can use set_reflog_action helper function in [1mgit-sh-setup [22mto set its name to this variable when it is invoked as[m
           the top level command by the end user, to be recorded in the body of the reflog.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_REF_PARANOIA[0m[m
           If this Boolean environment variable is set to false, ignore broken or badly named refs when iterating over lists of refs. Normally Git will try to include any such refs, which may cause[m
           some operations to fail. This is usually preferable, as potentially destructive operations (e.g., [1mgit-prune[22m(1)) are better off aborting rather than ignoring broken refs (and thus considering[m
           the history they point to as not worth saving). The default value is [1m1 [22m(i.e., be paranoid about detecting and aborting all operations). You should not normally need to set this to [1m0[22m, but it[m
           may be useful when trying to salvage data from a corrupted repository.[m
[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 1080 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       [1mGIT_COMMIT_GRAPH_PARANOIA[0m[m
           When loading a commit object from the commit-graph, Git performs an existence check on the object in the object database. This is done to avoid issues with stale commit-graphs that contain[m
           references to already-deleted commits, but comes with a performance penalty.[m
[m
           The default is "false", which disables the aforementioned behavior. Setting this to "true" enables the existence check so that stale commits will never be returned from the commit-graph at[m
           the cost of performance.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_ALLOW_PROTOCOL[0m[m
           If set to a colon-separated list of protocols, behave as if [1mprotocol.allow [22mis set to [1mnever[22m, and each of the listed protocols has [1mprotocol.[4m[22m<name>[24m[1m.allow [22mset to [1malways [22m(overriding any existing[m
           configuration). See the description of [1mprotocol.allow [22min [1mgit-config[22m(1) for more details.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_PROTOCOL_FROM_USER[0m[m
           Set this Boolean environment variable to false to prevent protocols used by fetch/push/clone which are configured to the [1muser [22mstate. This is useful to restrict recursive submodule[m
           initialization from an untrusted repository or for programs which feed potentially-untrusted URLS to git commands. See [1mgit-config[22m(1) for more details.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_PROTOCOL[0m[m
           For internal use only. Used in handshaking the wire protocol. Contains a colon [4m:[24m separated list of keys with optional values [4m<key>[=<value>][24m. Presence of unknown keys and values must be[m
           ignored.[m
[m
           Note that servers may need to be configured to allow this variable to pass over some transports. It will be propagated automatically when accessing local repositories (i.e., [1mfile:// [22mor a[m
           filesystem path), as well as over the [1mgit:// [22mprotocol. For git-over-http, it should work automatically in most configurations, but see the discussion in [1mgit-http-backend[22m(1). For[m
           git-over-ssh, the ssh server may need to be configured to allow clients to pass this variable (e.g., by using [1mAcceptEnv GIT_PROTOCOL [22mwith OpenSSH).[m
[m
           This configuration is optional. If the variable is not propagated, then clients will fall back to the original "v0" protocol (but may miss out on some performance improvements or features).[m
           This variable currently only affects clones and fetches; it is not yet used for pushes (but may be in the future).[m
[m
       [1mGIT_OPTIONAL_LOCKS[0m[m
           If this Boolean environment variable is set to false, Git will complete any requested operation without performing any optional sub-operations that require taking a lock. For example, this[m
           will prevent [1mgit status [22mfrom refreshing the index as a side effect. This is useful for processes running in the background which do not want to cause lock contention with other operations on[m
           the repository. Defaults to [1m1[22m.[m
[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 1111 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       [1mGIT_REDIRECT_STDIN[22m, [1mGIT_REDIRECT_STDOUT[22m, [1mGIT_REDIRECT_STDERR[0m[m
           Windows-only: allow redirecting the standard input/output/error handles to paths specified by the environment variables. This is particularly useful in multi-threaded applications where the[m
           canonical way to pass standard handles via [1mCreateProcess[22m() is not an option because it would require the handles to be marked inheritable (and consequently [1mevery [22mspawned process would[m
           inherit them, possibly blocking regular Git operations). The primary intended use case is to use named pipes for communication (e.g. \\.\pipe\my-git-stdin-123).[m
[m
           Two special values are supported: [1moff [22mwill simply close the corresponding standard handle, and if [1mGIT_REDIRECT_STDERR [22mis [1m2[22m>&1, standard error will be redirected to the same handle as[m
           standard output.[m
[m
       [1mGIT_PRINT_SHA1_ELLIPSIS [22m(deprecated)[m
           If set to [1myes[22m, print an ellipsis following an (abbreviated) SHA-1 value. This affects indications of detached HEADs ([1mgit-checkout[22m(1)) and the raw diff output ([1mgit-diff[22m(1)). Printing an[m
           ellipsis in the cases mentioned is no longer considered adequate and support for it is likely to be removed in the foreseeable future (along with the variable).[m
[m
       [1mGIT_ADVICE[0m[m
           If set to [1m0[22m, then disable all advice messages. These messages are intended to provide hints to human users that may help them get out of problematic situations or take advantage of new[m
           features. Users can disable individual messages using the [1madvice.[22m* config keys. These messages may be disruptive to tools that execute Git processes, so this variable is available to disable[m
           the messages. (The [1m--no-advice [22mglobal option is also available, but old Git versions may fail when this option is not understood. The environment variable will be ignored by Git versions[m
           that do not understand it.)[m

[1mDISCUSSION[0m[m
       More detail on the following is available from the [34m[1mGit concepts chapter of the user-manual[0m[1m[22m[3] and [1mgitcore-tutorial[22m(7).[m
[m
       A Git project normally consists of a working directory with a ".git" subdirectory at the top level. The .git directory contains, among other things, a compressed object database representing the[m
       complete history of the project, an "index" file which links that history to the current contents of the working tree, and named pointers into that history such as tags and branch heads.[m
[m
       The object database contains objects of three main types: blobs, which hold file data; trees, which point to blobs and other trees to build up directory hierarchies; and commits, which each[m
       reference a single tree and some number of parent commits.[m
[m
       The commit, equivalent to what other systems call a "changeset" or "version", represents a step in the project‚Äôs history, and each parent represents an immediately preceding step. Commits with[m
       more than one parent represent merges of independent lines of development.[m
[m
       All objects are named by the SHA-1 hash of their contents, normally written as a string of 40 hex digits. Such names are globally unique. The entire history leading up to a commit can be vouched[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 1142 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K       for by signing just that commit. A fourth object type, the tag, is provided for this purpose.[m
[m
       When first created, objects are stored in individual files, but for efficiency may later be compressed together into "pack files".[m
[m
       Named pointers called refs mark interesting points in history. A ref may contain the SHA-1 name of an object or the name of another ref (the latter is called a "symbolic ref"). Refs with names[m
       beginning [1mrefs/head/ [22mcontain the SHA-1 name of the most recent commit (or "head") of a branch under development. SHA-1 names of tags of interest are stored under [1mrefs/tags/[22m. A symbolic ref named[m
       [1mHEAD [22mcontains the name of the currently checked-out branch.[m
[m
       The index file is initialized with a list of all paths and, for each path, a blob object and a set of attributes. The blob object represents the contents of the file as of the head of the[m
       current branch. The attributes (last modified time, size, etc.) are taken from the corresponding file in the working tree. Subsequent changes to the working tree can be found by comparing these[m
       attributes. The index may be updated with new content, and new commits may be created from the content stored in the index.[m
[m
       The index is also capable of storing multiple entries (called "stages") for a given pathname. These stages are used to hold the various unmerged version of a file when a merge is in progress.[m
[m
[1mSECURITY[0m[m
       Some configuration options and hook files may cause Git to run arbitrary shell commands. Because configuration and hooks are not copied using [1mgit clone[22m, it is generally safe to clone remote[m
       repositories with untrusted content, inspect them with [1mgit log[22m, and so on.[m
[m
       However, it is not safe to run Git commands in a [1m.git [22mdirectory (or the working tree that surrounds it) when that [1m.git [22mdirectory itself comes from an untrusted source. The commands in its config[m
       and hooks are executed in the usual way.[m
[m
       By default, Git will refuse to run when the repository is owned by someone other than the user running the command. See the entry for [1msafe.directory [22min [1mgit-config[22m(1). While this can help protect[m
       you in a multi-user environment, note that you can also acquire untrusted repositories that are owned by you (for example, if you extract a zip file or tarball from an untrusted source). In such[m
       cases, you‚Äôd need to "sanitize" the untrusted repository first.[m
[m
       If you have an untrusted [1m.git [22mdirectory, you should first clone it with [1mgit clone --no-local [22mto obtain a clean copy. Git does restrict the set of options and hooks that will be run by[m
       [1mupload-pack[22m, which handles the server side of a clone or fetch, but beware that the surface area for attack against [1mupload-pack [22mis large, so this does carry some risk. The safest thing is to[m
       serve the repository as an unprivileged user (either via [1mgit-daemon[22m(1), ssh, or using other tools to change user ids). See the discussion in the [1mSECURITY [22msection of [1mgit-upload-pack[22m(1).[m
[m
[1mFURTHER DOCUMENTATION[0m[m
       See the references in the "description" section to get started using Git. The following is probably more detail than necessary for a first-time user.[m
[01;47;34m Manual page git(1) line 1173 (press h for help or q to quit)[0m[K[K [KESCESC[K[[[K66[K~~[K[m
       The [34m[1mGit concepts chapter of the user-manual[0m[1m[22m[3] and [1mgitcore-tutorial[22m(7) both provide introductions to the underlying Git architecture.[m
[m
       See [1mgitworkflows[22m(7) for an overview of recommended workflows.[m
[m
       See also the [34m[1mhowto[0m[1m[22m[4] documents for some useful examples.[m
[m
       The internals are documented in the [34m[1mGit API documentation[0m[1m[22m[5].[m
[m
       Users migrating from CVS may also want to read [1mgitcvs-migration[22m(7).[m

       the list archive at [34m[1mhttps://lore.kernel.org/git [0m[1m[22mfor previous bug reports and other discussions.[m
[m
       Issues which are security relevant should be disclosed privately to the Git Security mailing list <[34m[1mgit-security@googlegroups.com[0m[1m[22m[7]>.[m
